## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: solid mechanics / materials science (constitutive stress–strain–temperature modeling)
**Analysis**: The variables are stress (sigma), strain (epsilon), and temperature (T), which strongly suggests a constitutive-law identification task in mechanics of materials. Typical relationships include elastic (often temperature-dependent modulus), thermoelastic strain offsets, and nonlinear/plastic/viscoelastic hardening with thermal softening.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke’s law (isothermal linear elasticity): sigma = c0 * epsilon (small-strain elastic regime)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (linear in T): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (stiffness changes with temperature)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (exponential softening/hardening): sigma = c0 * exp(c1 * T) * epsilon (rapid thermal dependence of elastic modulus)
- Thermoelastic stress with thermal strain offset: sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * (T - c2)) (constraint-induced stress from thermal expansion)
- Bilinear elastic–plastic (smooth approximation): sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * log(1 + exp(c2 * (epsilon - c3))) (elastic then post-yield tangent modulus)
- Hollomon/Ludwik-type strain hardening: sigma = c0 * (c1 + epsilon)^(c2) (plastic hardening vs strain; avoids singularity at epsilon=0)
- Ramberg–Osgood (implicit form): epsilon = c0 * sigma + c1 * sigma^(c2) (nonlinear elasticity/plasticity; sigma is solved from epsilon)
- Voce hardening (saturating flow stress): sigma = c0 + c1 * (1 - exp(-c2 * epsilon)) (hardening that asymptotes at large strain)
- Exponential stress–strain (rubber-like / nonlinear elastic proxy): sigma = c0 * (exp(c1 * epsilon) - 1) (strongly nonlinear stiffening)
- Thermal softening factor on a strain law: sigma = (c0 + c1 * (c2 + epsilon)^(c3)) * exp(-c4 * T) (flow stress decreases with temperature)
- Rational thermal softening (bounded, avoids constants in denominator): sigma = (c0 + c1 * (c2 + epsilon)^(c3)) * (c4 / (T + c5)) (softening ~ 1/T over a range)
- WLF-like temperature shift on modulus/strength (polymer-style): sigma = (c0 * epsilon) * exp(c1 * (T - c2) / (c3 + (T - c2))) (glassy–rubbery transition behavior via shift factor)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Small-strain elastic regime → sigma proportional to epsilon; deviations indicate nonlinear elasticity or early plasticity.
- Thermal softening of stiffness/strength → multiplicative decreasing factors in T such as exp(-c*T) or c/(T+c0).
- Thermal expansion under constraint → dependence on (epsilon - c*(T - T0)), i.e., a temperature-driven horizontal shift in the stress–strain curve.
- Plastic yielding onset → smooth hinge-like add-ons (e.g., log(1+exp(c*(epsilon-eps_y)))) that create a kink without discontinuity.
- Work hardening → power-law growth in (epsilon + offset)^(n), often with 0<n<1 for many metals in certain regimes.
- Saturating hardening → approach to an asymptote in epsilon via (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) (captures finite hardening capacity).
- Highly nonlinear stiffening (e.g., polymers/elastomers) → exponential-in-epsilon terms exp(c*epsilon) dominating at large strain.
- Coupled thermo-mechanical behavior → strain-law multiplied by a temperature factor (separable form f(epsilon)*g(T)) is common when T mainly scales strength.
- Transition-like temperature behavior (polymers) → rational-in-(T-T0) inside exponent (WLF-like) to model rapid changes near a reference temperature.
